<dsc reserve="629" >The SqlHelper class is intended to encapsulate high performance, scalable best practices for 
common uses of SqlClient. -The ConcreteProduct implements the Product interface.

 -The Singleton defines an Instance operation that lets clients access its unique instance. 
-It may be responsible for creating its own unique instance.

 -The ConcreteSubject stores state of interest to ConcreteObserver.
-It sends a notification to its Observers when its state changes.
 -The Subject knows its Observers. Any number of Observers may observe a Subject.
-It provides an interface for attaching and detaching Observer objects.
</dsc>
<nam>SqlHelper</nam>

<dsc reserve="536" >This method is used to attach array of SqlParameters to a SqlCommand.
This method will assign a value of DbNull to any parameter with a direction of
InputOutput and a value of null.  
This behavior will prevent default values from being used, but
this will be the less common case than an intended pure output parameter (derived as InputOutput)
where the user provided no input value.
Parameters:
-command - The command to which the parameters will be added
-commandParameters - an array of SqlParameters tho be added to command</dsc>

This behavior will prevent default values from being used, but
this will be the less common case than an intended pure output parameter (derived as InputOutput)
where the user provided no input value.

<dsc reserve="516" >Execute a SqlCommand (that returns no resultset and takes no parameters) against the database specified in 
the connection string. 
e.g.:  
Dim result as Integer =  ExecuteNonQuery(connString, CommandType.StoredProcedure, &quot;PublishOrders&quot;)
Parameters:
-connectionString - a valid connection string for a SqlConnection
-commandType - the CommandType (stored procedure, text, etc.)
-commandText - the stored procedure name or T-SQL command
Returns: an int representing the number of rows affected by the command</dsc>

<dsc reserve="628" >Execute a SqlCommand (that returns no resultset) against the database specified in the connection string 
using the provided parameters.
e.g.:

-commandType - the CommandType (stored procedure, text, etc.)
-commandText - the stored procedure name or T-SQL command
-commandParameters - an array of SqlParamters used to execute the command

<dsc reserve="498" >Execute a SqlCommand (that returns no resultset) against the database specified in the connection string 
using the provided parameters.
e.g.:  
Dim result as Integer = ExecuteNonQuery(connString, CommandType.StoredProcedure, &quot;PublishOrders&quot;, new SqlParameter(&quot;@prodid&quot;, 24))
Parameters:
-commandText - the stored procedure name or T-SQL command
-commandParameters - an array of SqlParamters used to execute the command
Returns: an int representing the number of rows affected by the command</dsc>

<dsc reserve="770" >Execute a stored procedure via a SqlCommand (that returns no resultset) against the database specified in 
the connection string using the provided parameter values.  This method will discover the parameters for the 
stored procedure, and assign the values based on parameter order.
This method provides no access to output parameters or the stored procedure's return value parameter.
e.g.:  
Dim result as Integer = ExecuteNonQuery(connString, &quot;PublishOrders&quot;, 24, 36)
Parameters:
-connectionString - a valid connection string for a SqlConnection
-spName - the name of the stored procedure
-parameterValues - an array of objects to be assigned as the input values of the stored procedure
Returns: an int representing the number of rows affected by the command</dsc>

<dsc reserve="756" >Execute a stored procedure via a SqlCommand (that returns a resultset) against the database specified in 
the connection string using the provided parameter values.  This method will discover the parameters for the 
stored procedure, and assign the values based on parameter order.
This method provides no access to output parameters or the stored procedure's return value parameter.
e.g.:  
Dim ds as Dataset= ExecuteDataset(connString, &quot;GetOrders&quot;, 24, 36)
Parameters:
-connectionString - a valid connection string for a SqlConnection
-spName - the name of the stored procedure
-parameterValues - an array of objects to be assigned as the input values of the stored procedure
Returns: a dataset containing the resultset generated by the command</dsc>

<dsc reserve="705" >Execute a stored procedure via a SqlCommand (that returns a resultset) against the specified
SqlTransaction using the provided parameter values.  This method will discover the parameters for the 
stored procedure, and assign the values based on parameter order.
This method provides no access to output parameters or the stored procedure's return value parameter.
e.g.:  
Dim ds As Dataset = ExecuteDataset(trans, &quot;GetOrders&quot;, 24, 36)
Parameters:
-transaction - a valid SqlTransaction 
-spName - the name of the stored procedure
-parameterValues - an array of objects to be assigned as the input values of the stored procedure
Returns: a dataset containing the resultset generated by the command</dsc>

<dsc reserve="846" >Create and prepare a SqlCommand, and call ExecuteReader with the appropriate CommandBehavior.
If we created and opened the connection, we want the connection to be closed when the DataReader is closed.
If the caller provided the connection, we want to leave it to them to manage.
Parameters:
-connection - a valid SqlConnection, on which to execute this command 
-transaction - a valid SqlTransaction, or 'null' 
-commandType - the CommandType (stored procedure, text, etc.) 
-commandText - the stored procedure name or T-SQL command 
-commandParameters - an array of SqlParameters to be associated with the command or 'null' if no parameters are required 
-connectionOwnership - indicates whether the connection parameter was provided by the caller, or created by SqlHelper 
Returns: SqlDataReader containing the results of the command</dsc>
<nam>ExecuteReader</nam>

<dsc reserve="715" >Execute a stored procedure via a SqlCommand (that returns a resultset) against the specified SqlConnection 
using the provided parameter values.  This method will discover the parameters for the 
stored procedure, and assign the values based on parameter order.
This method provides no access to output parameters or the stored procedure's return value parameter.
e.g.:  
Dim dr As SqlDataReader = ExecuteReader(conn, &quot;GetOrders&quot;, 24, 36)
Parameters:
-connection - a valid SqlConnection 
-spName - the name of the stored procedure 
-parameterValues - an array of objects to be assigned as the input values of the stored procedure 
Returns: a SqlDataReader containing the resultset generated by the command</dsc>

<dsc reserve="798" >Execute a stored procedure via a SqlCommand (that returns a 1x1 resultset) against the database specified in 
the connection string using the provided parameter values.  This method will discover the parameters for the 
stored procedure, and assign the values based on parameter order.
This method provides no access to output parameters or the stored procedure's return value parameter.
e.g.:  
Dim orderCount As Integer = CInt(ExecuteScalar(connString, &quot;GetOrderCount&quot;, 24, 36))
Parameters:
-connectionString - a valid connection string for a SqlConnection 
-spName - the name of the stored procedure 
-parameterValues - an array of objects to be assigned as the input values of the stored procedure 
Returns: an object containing the value in the 1x1 resultset generated by the command</dsc>

<RMS:LRF id="8qYhg/KKdkO5EhgvXE8Kmg" />
</tgd>
<val>Observer_Binding Pattern</val>
</stv>
<stv id="Yfy/vWrrck2ykE9R8DgZZw" >
<tgd>
<RMS:LRF id="mCIl0IJr1Uupw0EoXpUMLw" />
</tgd>
<val reserve="145" >Define a one-to-many dependency between objects so that when one object changes state, all its dependents are notified and updated automatically.</val>
</stv>
<stv id="6AEdZ/vG+UOgPE/VjChJSQ" >
<tgd>
<RMS:LRF id="GjzO6CgFCUeq2NvqwIWOmg" />
</tgd>
<val reserve="354" >Collaborations
ConcreteSubject notifies its Observers whenever a change occurs that could make its Observers' state inconsistent with its own.
After being informed of a change in the ConcreteSubject, a ConcreteObserver object may query the Subject for information. ConcreteObserver uses this information to reconcile its state with that of the Subject.</val>
</stv>
<ftv id="T0tWjXvU2UqeUzmYZfy1eg" >
<tgd>
<RMS:LRF id="81RuwF8fvkWoALmE/lxt7g" />
</tgd>
<val>
<RMS:LRF id="L/TC+bj0tkexJflAhuCuag" />
</val>
</ftv>

<tgd>
<RMS:LRF id="KMdx5/i1pU2FCqcu6WN7sw" />
</tgd>

<RMS:IRF id="R3eS+TVPTU+zRiDjER0HtQ"  name="GoFPatternLibrary::Behavioral Patterns::Observer"  classStr="pkx"  import="5" />
</val>

<tgd id="bxMtodkQFkiNaA8rdeTEDQ" >
<dsc reserve="468" >An optional single character-set modifier of an external method declaration, which governs the character set used to marshal strings during a call to the external method. The Unicode modifier marshals all strings to Unicode values, the Ansi modifier marshals all strings to ANSI values, and the Auto modifier marshals the strings according to COM+ rules based on the name of the method, or the alias name if specified. If no modifier is specified, the default is Ansi.</dsc>
<dri>164</dri>
